## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of concentration A, which is the central object in chemical kinetics. With only t and A available, the most common identifiable relationships are kinetic rate-law ODEs where dA_dt depends on A (reaction order, saturation, equilibrium relaxation) and possibly explicit time-dependence in the effective rate constant.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion when reagent is in excess or surface-limited)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay / pseudo-first-order kinetics)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or second-order overall in A)
- General nth-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (effective reaction order fit from data)
- Linear relaxation to baseline: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to an equilibrium/baseline concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating growth with depletion/limiting capacity)
- Mixed-order (sum of channels): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (parallel first- and second-order loss pathways)
- Rational saturation in A (limited-rate regime): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (rate increases ~A at low A but saturates at high A)
- Rational inhibition in A: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A**2) (self-inhibition / crowding-type slowdown at high A)
- Time-varying first-order coefficient (linear drift): dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * t) * A (changing conditions or catalyst activity varying over time)
- Time-varying first-order coefficient (exponential drift): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (accelerating/decelerating effective rate with time-dependent environment)
- Periodic forcing (e.g., light-driven): dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (externally modulated first-order loss such as photolysis with oscillatory intensity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is proportional to A (approximately straight line in dA_dt vs A), a first-order term -c*A is likely.
- If dA_dt scales like A**2 at higher A (curvature upward in magnitude vs A), include a second-order or higher-order term -c*A**n.
- A nonzero intercept in dA_dt vs A suggests a zero-order component (-c0) or an affine relaxation term -c*(A-c1).
- Sign change of dA_dt around a particular A indicates a stable fixed point A≈c1, motivating -c*(A-c1) or c*A*(c1-A).
- If |dA_dt| grows with A at low A but plateaus at high A, use rational saturation forms like -c*A/(1+c*A) rather than pure power laws.
- If decay is initially slow then speeds up (or vice versa) even at similar A, model explicit time dependence in the rate coefficient, e.g., -k(t)*A with k(t)=c*(1+c*t) or k(t)=c*exp(c*t).
- If residuals show periodic structure over t, incorporate sinusoidal modulation in the rate coefficient, e.g., (1+c*sin(c*t))*A.
- If multiple regimes appear (e.g., early-time linear-in-A then late-time stronger-than-linear), try additive pathways -c1*A - c2*A**2 to represent parallel mechanisms.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (CRK15)
============================================================
GT: -c0*sqrt(A) - c1*A*exp(-c2*_s*t) + c3*_t*sin(log(A + c4))
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed function of \(t,A\)):
\[
f(t,A)= -0.1207203443\,\sqrt{A}\;-\;0.1207203443\,A\,e^{-0.068623049\,t}\;+\;0.8537417103\,\sin(\log(A+1)).
\]
So GT contains three essential, non-removable functional “shapes”:
1) a \(\sqrt{A}\) term (no \(t\) dependence),
2) an \(A\exp(k t)\) term with \(k<0\),
3) a \(\sin(\log(A+1))\) term (no \(t\) dependence).

To match GT, a candidate must be able (by choosing its constants) to produce **all three** of these shapes and **no extra** unmatched dependence.

---

### Candidate 1
Form: linear in \(A\) + \(A^{c2}c3 e^{c4 t}\) + rational \(c5/(A+c6)\) + constant + \(c8\log(Ac9+1)\).
- Has no \(\sqrt{A}\) term unless you set \(A^{c2}\) to \(\sqrt{A}\) (i.e., \(c2=1/2\)), but that term is multiplied by \(e^{c4 t}\), so it would depend on \(t\) unless \(c4=0\). If \(c4=0\), then you lose the required \(A e^{kt}\) term.
- Also only has \(\log(\cdot)\), not \(\sin(\log(\cdot))\).
⇒ Cannot match.

### Candidate 2
Similar issues: only \(\log\), no \(\sin(\log)\); only one power-exponential term \(A^{c1}e^{c3 t}\) so can’t simultaneously create \(\sqrt{A}\) (no \(t\)) and \(A e^{kt}\) (with \(t\)).
⇒ Cannot match.

### Candidate 3
Same as 2 plus an \(A\) term; still no \(\sin(\log)\) and cannot get both \(\sqrt{A}\) (no \(t\)) and \(A e^{kt}\) from a single \(A^{c1}e^{c3 t}\) term.
⇒ Cannot match.

### Candidate 4
Has \(A^{c1}e^{c3 t}\), rational, and \(\log\) (not sine). Same structural mismatch.
⇒ Cannot match.

### Candidate 5
Has one \(A^{c3}e^{c5 t}\) term and \(\log\) (not sine). Also has only rational-in-\(A\) besides linear terms; no way to create \(\sin(\log(A+1))\).
⇒ Cannot match.

### Candidate 6
Same core issue: no \(\sin(\log)\); only one power-exponential term so can’t produce both \(\sqrt{A}\) (no \(t\)) and \(A e^{kt}\).
⇒ Cannot match.

GT: -c0*sqrt(A) - c1*A*exp(-c2*_s*t) + c3*_t*sin(log(A + c4))

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.12072*sqrt(A) - 0.12072*A*exp(-0.06862*t) + 0.85374*sin(log(A + 1))`

The GT has three basis functions:
1. `sqrt(A)` — i.e., `A^0.5`
2. `A*exp(c*t)` — with negative exponent coefficient
3. `sin(log(A + 1))`

Key observations:
- The GT contains `sin(log(A+1))`, which is a very specific nonlinear function
- The GT contains `sqrt(A)` = `A^0.5`
- The GT contains `A*exp(c*t)`

Let me check each candidate for the presence of these basis functions.

**Critical check:** Does any candidate contain `sin(log(...))` or equivalent? Let me scan all candidates:

- Candidate 41 has `sin(A*c4 + c5)` — this is `sin` of a linear function of A, NOT `sin(log(A+1))`. These are fundamentally different functions. **NO MATCH**.

None of the candidates contain `sin(log(...))`. Let me check if any candidate could somehow produce `sin(log(A+1))` through some algebraic manipulation.

Looking at the candidates, they use combinations of:
- `A*c`, `A^c`, `exp(A*c)`, `log(A*c+1)`, `exp(c*t)`, `1/(A+c)`, `A/(A+c)`, `tanh(...)`, `sin(A*c+c)`, `t^c`, `1/(c+t)`, `t/(ct+c)`

None of these can produce `sin(log(A+1))`. The function `sin(log(A+1))` is linearly independent from all the basis functions present in the candidates (polynomials in A, exponentials in A, logarithms in A, rational functions in A, etc.).

Specifically:
- `log(A*c + 1)` ≠ `sin(log(A + 1))` — logarithm vs sine of logarithm
- `exp(A*c)` cannot approximate `sin(log(A+1))` exactly
- `sin(A*c + c)` ≠ `sin(log(A+1))` — sine of linear vs sine of log
- No combination of the available basis functions can exactly equal `sin(log(A+1))`

Since `sin(log(A+1))` has coefficient 0.85374 (not negligible), and no candidate contains this basis function or any equivalent, **no candidate can match the GT**.
